=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Rating respective of the flexibility offered by various expansions, but even the core game is wildly fun and kept me up at night thinking about it when I first played (likely an 8). 
 
Core Game: Turn-order and player-power auction to open every round. Incremental expansion, focus on city-building.

Hades: Incremental expansion with a period of brutal war. A second tier of deities and a fleet of heroes add some additional play elements to both broaden the gameplay and soften some of the more unfair surprise win conditions.

Titans: Goes from naval war to land-war with a secondary mechanic to speed troop moving. This is much closer to a Risk variant than to the original thoughtful game, but it's no worse for the transition.

C3K: Crashes game balance by importing the Kemet creatures and giving them balance breaking powers.

Full reviews on each expansion page. My favorite variant is Hades/Titans + Kemet creatures house-ruled to act as normal single-turn creature purchases (which also saves you from needing the miniatures).

With all the expansions in play the depth of this game is awesome while still playing quickly without too many points of decision paralysis outside of bidding.

Game components are wonderful except the cards, which are too cheap for how much they are handled. The edges on mine started wearing after two plays.

RATING: 8
A multiple victory condition game with a very interesting bidding mechanic. Aside from the Kraken, it's also an incredibly thematic game. Planning ahead is rewarded, but the bidding mechanic and available mythical creatures force you to always have a plan B.
Every single game we played, every player was within one, maximum two moves of victory. It's always so very close, and I love that.
Not a 10 point game though: the fun really decreases when playing with less than 4. The maps hold up just fine, and so do most mechanics, except for the bidding, which becomes much less intense.

RATING: N/A
In this latest collaboration between Bruno Cathala and Ludovic Maublanc, players must buy the favor of the gods in their race to be the first player to build two cities in the Ancient Greek island group known as the Cyclades.

Victory requires respect for all the gods - players cannot afford to sacrifice to only one god, but must pay homage to each of five gods in turn. Each turn, the players bid for the favors of the gods, as only one player can have the favor of each god per turn - and each player is also limited to the favor of a single god per turn.

RATING: 3
If you like auction/bidding games which are 100% euro style with a theme that makes no sense with the mechanics, then maybe you will like this game. But it's really not my case.

I don't think there is actually something buggy about this game, I just think that it's just boring. First because I hate auctions, Second because it seems like the kind of game where what ever you do, each player will end-up with almost the same score. So why bother playing.

The only surprising thing in this game is that there is no victory points. Surprising for a euro game.

So the map is somewhat optional. They could have given each player an island board like in Puerto Rico, and the results would have been similar.

RATING: 9
It's "Euro-trash" (part Ameri-Trash and part-Euro).  There are Gods to bid favors from and acquire special powers with, Mythic Monsters to call upon, a navy of ships to move, armies to build/conquer with and special buildings to erect.  Lots of opportunity, planning, quick-changing strategies and counter-strategies.  Cyclades is quick and dynamic, things change quickly.  It takes off like a ski-shoot but many times, climatic finishes can end abruptly like driving off a cliff (when you least expect it).  I rather enjoy the ride of this if you like Euro-wargames.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Cyclades is a fantastic and exciting game. At first glance it looks like a wargame set in a mythological setting, but it is much more than that. It has elements of wargaming, area control but mostly it's an auction/bidding game. To execute certain actions you need to make an offer to a specific God. This is the heart of the game and its the moment where players most often butt heads. An all round great game that plays with a full compliment of players in 60 to 90 minutes. And I hear that the Titans expansion makes this even better. 

Update 10/'15: After having only played four games I'm upping the score to a 9.5. I love this game. Every element works so well together. The final rounds are incredibly tense as all players are scrambling to be the first to build their metropolises. A fantastic game that gets better after every play. 

Update 01/'18: Cyclades is still a great game but it doesn't hit the table all that often anymore. A lot of recent games have done what Cyclades did much better. The bidding mechanisms still make this unique so it'll stay in my collection. Lowered to an 8.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[u]Comments:[/u]
Cyclades is something like a Game of Thrones light, or at least that is how it feels to me. A Dudes On A Map facade is used to hide a bidding and role selection game that has some really interesting things going on. The game is pretty thematic with players taking on the role of Greek city states fighting for dominance in the region. To win the game players must fight off mythical creatures (a very cool element to the game) and each other to build two Metropolis'. The trick is that you can only do one type of thing each tround because bid on the favor of the gods, and only one god will bless you with the favor each round (i.e. Ares gives you troops, and lets you attack other players). The Gods also let you build one of each of the required buildings you need to build a Metropolis. 

Presented with many different paths to victory this game is a mix of Euro and Amerirtrash that pulls off what it sets out to do, and that is simply to be a fun game. 

If you aren't having fun when you are playing and get to say "Release the Kraken" then you don't know how to have fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
- Everybody was tempted by this game, because it looks very good.

* First game, with 3 players:

- After 8 turns: none of us was very impressed with the game play, so far.  I do not feel any tension.  I don't make so many plans, in part because having only a few gods makes plans longer to execute, and I would be more interested if I could put them into fruition faster.  Maybe I am not spending enough time thinking and strategizing: I tend to lead and animate the game, to the detriment of my investment in it.  Evan is not very focused, which does not helped (he complained about not winning a few auctions, and left the table on 2 or 3 occasions).  However, things are starting to get more interesting, as we can see some of us getting closer to their first metropolis, and also because we are starting to have more significant revenues and, therefore, possibilities.  We also started finding the creatures useful, with the more developed board situation.

- Turns 8-12: The last part of the game was more interesting.  We went through all the creatures.  We used many of them, and it was nice to see what possibilities opened up.  We also started to make invasion plans, etc., thanks to the more crowded board, and to the fact that we were starting to get the hang of the mechanics.  Evan pulled off a victory in a way that we overlooked, because we had forgotten to read the Chimera's special power until the action phase; Evan used it to invade an island with a fortress on it with Pegasus, and he got a metropolis this way.

- Conclusion: after being a little disappointed, I started to like the game.  At first, I felt a little like with Small World: nice, varied bits; simple rules; but not many interesting decisions, because of a relative lack of tension.  Then, we started to make more plans, and to bother each other.  I think we would like the game even better if we all used more time to make plans, instead of leaving the table (Evan), dreaming a little (Jane) or keeping things moving (me).  I suggested this, and this worked (and could have worked better with a greater general involvement).  However, I did miss the interactivity brought about by Settlers, with its constant exchanges (Cosmic Encounter is not bad either at that).

* Second game, with 2 players:

It took us 2 hours to play: in the same time frame, I prefer the wild variety of Magic, the story and streamlined intricacies of Clockwork Wars, the richer combats and situations of A Few Acres of Snow. Maybe this is a good game to keep for more players, though (it even does 5 players): it has the interactive, area control element and miniatures with special powers of Blood Rage (but not the building of a tableau of special powers). But then I have Clockwork Wars for this, or Cry Havoc for 4 people. Maybe this is a game which is in a similar category as Inis, for instance. Maybe my Cry Havoc is good enough for multiplayer combat, though, and better for 2 player? In any case, for 2 players, I prefer to play Hellas: it has a similar combat element, but adds exploration, and more special powers and surprises.

=> I guess I should sell it, I don't see much use for it, except as a diversion from the other, better games. But then I don't play those games with many people often.

RATING: 6
For an auction game this game has mechanics to make it work decently with low numbers. However, attacking seems pretty cumbersome and expensive in this game (not saying there isn't an incentive because it is highly profitable to do so, only that it physically can't happen that often), as you will probably need at least 2 turns to create a string of ships and follow up with moving your armies across to the other island. 

This game seems to suffer a bit from runaway leader though, as despite the monetary bonus from Apollo for being behind if you control more islands, if you are ahead you'll have more income from having more islands, and then you can camp whichever god is first each round to use all the mythological creatures (need some more plays in the higher player counts to see if this is also true for 4-5). Components are very nice and each color has different model sculpts (it's also both fun and profitable to unleash the Kraken). 

I am afraid this game will suffer from replayability issues, as the change in mythological creatures/gods per turn while important doesn't seem to the experience completely different from game to game.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
The best combination of auction and area control mechanics into a wargame. Also the theme: mythology creates some beautiful artwork. 

The game is very easy to learn because it doesn't have an excessive amount of rules. Basically a player can learn it on the first play.

Because is a wargame it involves strategy but, unlike other wargames a player can't plan the strategy from the beginning, instead players come up with the strategy when they see an opportunity. Also the strategies are not extremely complex so anyone can play this game but there are many ways to win.

Also it has very beautiful game components: 
- the map looks like an exotic wallpaper 
- each player ships and soldiers not only that have different colors but have also different models for each color
- high detailed miniatures specially those five big mythological creatures.
- irregular shaped cardboard coins with two different faces.

Advantages:
- superb combination of auction with area control
- high quality and very good looking game components
- very nice theme
- easy to learn
- works just as well in two player mode as in more than two (different rules in 1 vs 1)
- lots of wining strategies
- very entertaining

Disadvantages:
- some rules are not explained very well (for example when a player discard a mythological creature)
- although it is a good idea to use symbols instead of text to display what a creature does, the symbols are kinda strange.
- those five mythological creatures that are so beautifully shaped are used maxim one round then they go off the board until next time a player buys them (except the kraken which remains on the board). It would have been nicer to stay a little longer even if no player would have benefit from them (like kraken).
- kinda hard to find where to buy the game because it is out of stock ... at least in Europe.

RATING: 6
Didn't do a great deal for me on the first play with 3 players, but it was quite quick.

Second game with 5 players really dig drag a bit, and the endgame was a slightly unsatisfying sneak rush to victory - not a great sign that I didn't really care that I'd won. Biggest issue for me was that none of the decisions I faced felt particularly interesting, because you ultimately have quite limited control over your own destiny. I suppose another way of saying that is there is luck involved, and screwage. Your strategy can easily be undone in an instant by particular cards coming up or by the roll of the dice, which some might enjoy as 'tension' and/or ensuring all players have a chance of victory, but for me just removes the purpose/reward of plotting a long-term strategy. And if a game lasts as long as this one, for me it *needs* deeper strategy than Cyclades can offer.

Assuming players will always seek to deny each other victory where possible, I can see most games ending only when a particular combination of unstoppable god auction order/monster cards comes up, and finally the player who has used in-game positioning or meta-game chat to avoid a bashing can sneak home. As a result it's all a bit 'meh', and there might be an argument for starting with an accelerated setup of some kind just to reach the inevitable endgame scenario more quickly. My suspicion (hope?) is 4 players will be better than 5, purely because it must reduce playing time. Looking around at other comments, it seems we weren't the only ones to suffer massively extended playing time. Also agree with comments elsewhere that some of the creatures are extremely powerful compared with others. Whether you define that as 'broken' or not, not sure.

Best features are probably the different miniature shapes between factions and the monster miniatures, it all looks very nice. Some miniatures seemed fragile though and a number arrived twisted.

Final thought: seems more than the average share of people have put no comment beside high ratings, I wonder if they have just been won over by the theme on a couple of plays and without thinking given it a (large) benefit of the doubt?
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.8
Somewhat intriguing game, just seems like its been done before.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Matagot have proven time and again that they know how to produce a gorgeous looking game with great bits and beautiful artwork, and Cyclades is no exception. The sculpted minis can get a bit warped out of the box (the softer plastic breaks less easily, but can be warped over time) but this is fixed easily with the application of some boiling water.

As a game, Cyclades is an interesting blend of Euro mechanics (it is primarily an auction-driven game) with some direct-conflict. The loaded dice mean that combat is never too deterministic, but also that a smaller army will reliably be defeated.

I love how the auction mechanic works. When a player is outbid for a given god's favour, he must choose a different god to bid on - you can't just enter a higher bid. This forces players to think more about how much to offer. Sometimes you'll want to bid high to ensure you get the god you want, sometimes you'll want to bid low in the hopes of being outbid, either to have a chance of seeing what others are up to, or to simply get another chance to bid on a god you were outbid on.

There are many paths to victory in this game, which means that players have to pay close attention - a careless player won't even realise that someone is about to win until they do! This should stand up well to repeated play.

RATING: 8
The more I play this game the more I enjoy it. Every choice you make pushes the game towards inevitable conflict. The initial placement of troops puts players into immediate tension. The shared need to take limited actions results in bidding wars. Acquiring buildings or cornucopias strengthens your position, but also makes you a more tantalizing target. I love the design. And Matagot's game production is amazing. The art, board, and miniatures are outstanding. Let me sing the praise of the immense monster figures. And each player color gets different sculpts for the armies and ships! This is a game that is sumptuous on every level.

RATING: 6
I wanted to enjoy Cyclades, but sadly this game seems to suffer from an identity crisis and mechanics that weren’t well tested.

For starters, with experienced players, it can easily go beyond 3 hours because everyone is scheming to block each other from winning.  You aren’t giving much options to win the game and it’s pretty obvious what your next turn is going to be.  Because of this transparency and lack of options, games either bog down to attrition or someone grabs Pegasus.

I’ve tried the Hades expansion, which was garbage, and also the Titans expansion, which improved the game but I felt that they are far better options out there.

RATING: 7
Possible trade - need to play it again.

Another fun and well balanced hybrid. What's particularly noteworthy about this is the way in which conflict is used as a threat to drive the play rather than being a factor in and of itself: because you need to spend at least 2 turns lining up an attack it's not hard to prepare a defence of some sort so actual battles are fairly rare. But you still get plenty of interaction & metagame because players have to respond to the *threat* of attack yet the game as a whole stays balanced. Excellent production values and plenty of variety. Big downside is that early quarter of game is quite dull as there's no value in early conflict and all the gods are valuable so auction lacks tension. But it certainly comes alive later on!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Combat in slow motion. Trying to figure out just how to perform your invasion in this game is a challenge - as you need to first set up your boats then send in the troops - and with 4 players you can't even be sure if you'll get the god you need from round to round. The result is tension, and a continuous struggle for more money so that you can better leverage the auctions. Ah, yes auctions - a great system of musical chairs with bidding - getting what you want for a reasonable price is tricky and can be dangerous - if you overextend you will be hurting down the line.

The end condition is good, great even, but I also suspect it is the most flawed part of the game and a part that the Titans expansion goes to great lengths to fix. The game relies on players building metropolises - but the only god that automatically drives the game towards this direction is Athena, so if everyone wants to lurk and wait to pounce on other players' metropolises (metropoli?) the game will grind to a halt. There just isn't enough incentive to build and risk it being taken away. 

The result is a good fast paced combat came that allows for cleverness, but is susceptible to becoming a drawn out affair or ending anticlimactically if everyone is not doing their share of "balancing" the game out (ensuring that a winning player can't just grab the one god they need to win).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Game in a Nutshell: Build your cities, while bribing gods, hiring mythological creatures for dastardly deeds, and battling for territory.

Played as: 5 player.

Pros: Includes my favorite type of auction (Amun-Re, Vegas Showdown, etc.) into a game that has some "civ-building", and hostile takeovers. The very limited amount of troops and ships force action and limits turtling. I like that the game allows for very different ways to the winning goal; either peacefully build, or take over the aforementioned buildings through force. Artwork and minis make for a nicely presented experience. 

Cons: The iconography is laughably bad (literally, it can be hilarious), making the included reference sheet an essential game component. The game end seems a bit anticlimactic as win conditions are open, leaders may be ganged up on, results become inevitable, etc. 

Other: My one play of this was LATE on the last night of a convention... who knows what a day-light play might do to my opinion of the game. My guess is that I'd enjoy it more and evolve with additional plays. I wonder how annoying luck would play into the game with less than 5 players when certain roles (maybe necessary to you) are randomly left out each round.

Best Use: A Euro for those who want some in-your-face, and theme slapped on it.

RATING: 5.5
Cyclades has a fun theme with Greek Gods, monsters and the chrome to support them.  However, when it comes to game play some problems arise.  First off the game seems to reward conservative play.  Once you get ahead, especially if you've built a Metropolis, you have a huge target on your back and your opponents have enough super powers (through the monsters) to quickly set you back.  It seems you don't want to make your big move until you're pretty sure you are going to win.  So instead you increase your economic engine, build up Philosophers (which do nothing for you except help you win the game) and turtle in the middle of the pack.  

After the slow build, once you've saved up enough money, you strike and hope someone doesn't muck up your plans with some crazy monster power.  I like simple fighting systems but unfortunately, in Cyclades, the monsters are rarely part of them so the battles are largely unspectacular.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game is exceptionally high on theme and production values: players play as warriors who bribe gods to get special powers.  The goal is to be the first player to control two of the biggest buildings; there are no victory points, and there's no second place.  

To get the biggest buildings players must either build four of the smaller buildings, get four philosopher cards, or attack another player and take over the building.  

The bidding system is fairly simple: the gods are randomly arranged on a track, and players bid how much gold they will bribe a certain god.  Whenever a player is outbid for a god, they must immediately bid on another god.  This system is interesting, but a bit frustrating, since you can't re-bid on the same god (making it tough to get what you want).

The game is relatively short (about an hour and a half for 4 players), though the rules are complicated enough that they also take a while.  

The game is a bit too random for my tastes: battles are highly random (dice rolls are a huge factor in close battles), and if a player isn't able to get income early in the game, then they're dead (as income is key to everything in the game).  

Overall a fine game, and one with great miniatures, but not stellar.  I'd prefer a straight-up war game or a straight euro.

RATING: 6
Very simple, yet loaded with subtleties that make the overall experience very rewarding. An excellent gateway to more advanced strategy games due to a combination of very good presentation with solid and straightforward mechanics. Highly recommended for players who want to take a shot at more complicated territory control games, but are afraid of the steep learning curve,

EDIT:

Having played the game a number of times, I reckon that most of the time there is not much going on. It's tough to wage war beause only one player can win Ares/Poseidon at a time, and while war is not the only way to win the game, then again the whole experience seems rather slow-paced and tough to control in the long run. Fun as it is, it doesn't even come close to serious strategy / war games.

EDIT: The expansion alleviates most of the issues I used to have with Cyclades and makes the whole experience deeper and aggressive. A very nice expansion indeed.

FINAL EDIT: OK, the expansion made it a good game again, but... There are so many other, better games to play - games that don't drag because of the bidding process and allow you to do what you want and when you want to do it. Thus, Cyclades has had to wave its goodbye after all.

RATING: 7.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Cyclades is a really interesting conflict game in that there is a fair dose of Euro in there as well...more than Nexus Ops even.

What separates Cyclades from other modern conflict designs is that various Gods must be bid on in an open auction format (think Amun-Re) and each Greek God offers up specific powers that correlate to combat, economics or construction of key buildings needed to win the game.

What really does it for me though is the wide variety of mythological beasts that can be drawn to your cause. There are lesser and greater beasts and each has a specific power that can be used to further your ends.

The action in Cyclades takes place in an area of ocean dotted by islands. Islands that are controlled can earn income and a base from which to launch attacks but also to build important buildings. 

The game really requires it's players to adapt to changes quickly and those beasts really can throw up major surprises. Strong leaders do need to be double or triple teamed at times to bring them down as having a big income affords a person great power. This concerns me somewhat so further play is required.

RATING: 9
Out of the civilization games I've played this seems to be the simplest one to learn. Cyclades is actually an auction game in which the players are bidding for the favor of the gods. For example you need the favor of Ares to recruit soldiers and go to war. That makes it very unique compared to other civ games.

In order to win you need to hold a certain number of metropolises. These cost a lot of resources to build. They do offer some defensive advantages, but keep in mind that building a metropolis is painting a target on your forehead so make sure the timing is right before you do it. I've heard that one of the expansions tries to fix this issue by making it more advantageous to build the first metropolis, so I'd like to try that expansion later.

Still a very good game, though. I recommend it, and the Greek mythology theme is a bonus!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
I really love this game's balance between auction mechanics and conquest/conflict between the players. I feel that this not only belongs in the strategy category, but also the theme category - each of the gods and their effects are very thematic, and it creates a sort of narrative of war between the players and rulers.

I do have some small complaints though - the game can get VERY tug-of-war-y where you get an island or metropolis and you lose it to other players, you get it back, and you lose it again. While I like this, sometimes games can start to get a bit long due to this. I sort of wish there was a built in timer for ending the game (maybe something like don't reshuffle when Chimera comes out and game ends when creature deck runs out and assign points based on islands/GP/buildings/cards controlled if no one has reached 2 Metropolises). I can deal without a timer mechanism but some of my friends have more trouble with the length as it can run into 3 hour long games (on the reverse side, I've finished in 1 hour as well). Another issue I have is Zeus' ability to cycle through monsters indefinitely and Pegasus swinging some games (this can be fixed if you want by limiting Zeus to only 3 or so Monster Lightning Bolts or having Pegasus only able to carry 2 soldiers, but I generally dislike using non-official variants).

I also found the double pillar variants for 3P/4P to be superior to vanilla 3/4P and the Pegasus limitation rule to be better balanced. That combined with the module for variable placement makes this game better but some people I play with don't want to play with different rules, and I am not crazy for variants either. 

Anyway, overall, this game had too many flaws for me to keep overlooking and trying to enjoy. 

In summary, its theme and components are great and its gameplay decent, but the weaknesses of dice combat, Pegasus, extremely long length and other things make this not enjoyable for me anymore.

RATING: 8
Civilization game, my ass.  The scale is far too small, the mythological elements far too prevalent.  Cyclades is a fight.  Cyclades is a race in which tripping, shoving, and tackling on the way to the finish line are not only legal but positively encouraged.  There are a few very basic upgrades you can buy and a handful of ways you can spend gold.  If this is all it takes to qualify for the civ game category, then half the Euro games in existence meet the criteria.

Cyclades is a fun game that doesn't take too long, has the right amount of stuff going on, and is a sumptuous feast for the eyes.  That's more than enough.  There's no need to pretend it is something that it clearly is not.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
First impression (4 players): I'm not the biggest fan of this type of games with quite a punch of hitting of other players. Cyclades was one of the better games in this genre. Here the game at least cannot stall for too long time and goes on all the time. This is achieved by the fact that every round there will be one token placed that increases someones income (and makes attacking a bit more tempting). Also the victory condition is relatively simple, build (or steal) two metropolises. As you can do Metropolises in two different ways too it's quite flexible. 

So far so good but unfortunately there is something negative too. There are 3 creatures to be purchased during every round and they cost 2/3/4 money but you can get price reduction to them. If you have two of those you can buy whole row for just 4 money and the powers are quite a bit powerful. So it can happen that you get a good god to bribe and on top of this 1 or 2 or even 3 monster powers you can get during some turns. Some other turn there might be much less wanted god and pretty crappy monsters. These swings can be quite big and who gets them is quite a bit determined by luck. Of course you make your luck by not spending too much money on previous round but this is not always possible.

To me personally it is bothering in this type of games that it can be very small things that in the end determine the winner. Here it can be one critical battle at some point during the game that really swings game to someones favour as margins in battles are pretty low.

RATING: 7
I think when I play this game more I'll have a higher rating to give this game.

This is an auction, area-control, light war-game.  In Cyclades you take command of a small army and an island or two depending on how many players there are.  Taking islands mean you gain more dosh per cycle.

the game looks complicated, but it is actually very very simple.  Everything is taken in steps and usually there's always something to do or consider.

The first step is to collect revenue for your territories.  Then players auction for the God's favor.  The auction phase ends when all players have a bid on one God each.  Each God grants something, even the free God, Apollo.

On everyone's turn they decide to take an action or recruit depending on which God they gained favor with that turn.  

The objective of the game?  To build 2 Metropolis'.

So what's bad about the game?  Not much really.  The dice can really make you win a battle that looks like you should of won otherwise, but in the theme of tactical warfare one can argue it emulates the risk and rewards of battle.

Each game I've seen won so far has been the first two players who build a Metropolis enter a massive war consisting of 1-3 battles where the victor takes over their opponent's Metropolis and win.  It feels that those who stay quiet and gain an early lead usually dominate the board.

The fights for islands themselves are my favorite part and the theme of the game really comes through when your Greek state annexes opponents.

RATING: 8
I played this recently again after quite some while, and have to revise my earlier judgement now. The game is actually very good and offers all the things I expect from a game I should like: it's interactive and thematically sound. Game play inevitably brings along some direct military confrontation, and a close finish. Play time is short but still Cyclades is a lot more than a filler. Also, there is a decent balancing mechanism (Apollo grants 4 gold if the player possesses only one island - BUT it fails with 3 or 2 players!). The rules are light, yet the game still feels comparably deep and challenging. It's far from being a brain burner, however - just a simple and interesting, yet not exhausting board game experience. Last but not least, it looks really beautiful.

What's also cool is that all players usually seem to have good chances for a surprising win. Sneaky victories shouldn't surprise you. 

With only 2 players, early luck determines the winner too quickly, with 3 players, it feels a bit lame. I'd recommend the game with 4 or even better 5.

RATING: 6
Nice art, good auction element, the theme is my favourite (ancient greece setting) but:
-has to be played with the right people (if you hate kingmaking or if you get your feelings hurt easily this game is not for you)
-3 player experience is not good (too few gods and the game drags)
-anticlimatic ending

I liked playing this game, because the auction mechanic is well done, but i had 2 games where I won and felt no sense of achievement, because I didn't deserve to win. One of the players was really smarter than anyone at the table, he was making the right decisions and making twice as much money than others, yet he still lost. Everyone turned on him with the mythical creatures (which are really inbalanced - infamous pegasus) and that gave me an opening for easy win (which I regreted almost seconds after the decision). For me the reason it suffers is because you need to accumulate only 2 vp (albeit 1 vp consists of several steps/parts) and there is no elimination (with a weird catch-up mechanism) and sporadic, yet very decisive conflict. Now, I generally  despise player elimination and like to avoid conflict, so I could just build and defend my empire, right? Wrong. It does not work in this game, simply because how impactful the combat could be. 
Every game I played went something like this: players build their empires, colonise islands and are roughly on the same level. After some time (1.5-2 hours) almost everybody has at least 1 metropolis (vp) and is either close to finishing second (2-3 turns from it) or has large enough military close to one of his opponents, that he can take it by force (with some luck or help of mythical creatures). Once everybody realizes this, the mayham begins and everybody tries to get the final point and the victory is usually granted to the one with the most luck in combat, or the player that for some reason was not attacked. It is all so sudden and random and undeserving and more often than not happens, that the player who was the best during the whole game gets attacked by everybody and somebody mediocre pulls of a victory by chance.
There is just too much chaos going on to feel that Your decisions matter and the turns feel slow (You cannot chain movements very efficiently).
It is simply a weird mix. I think I would have liked it more, if it were a pure euro, or even if it was a pure wargame. Even though I don't like conflict I feel that I would have liked this game more if it had more of it (It would have at least felt that You were fighting for survival, not just being unlucky in one battle that You had during one session)

RATING: 7
規則:
*根據人數放起始設定，生物卡洗勻放對應位置，哲學家卡跟祭司卡放對應位置
*每個人拿一個顏色所有配件跟5元(錢放屏幕後)，每個人拿一個柱隨機放置順位軌
*遊戲進行數輪直到輪結束時有玩家擁有兩座大城市獲勝(多人擁有比錢)，每輪有6階段
1.開生物卡 第一輪開一張放4，第二輪如果空了放3跟4，沒空就4移到3放4，之後就是2的移除，其他右移，在開滿
2.開神明版塊，5人隨機洗勻開，4人最後一張不開，下輪開並放到最上面在洗勻剩下的，最後一張在不開，3人開兩張，下輪換剩下兩張，在下輪在重洗，2人同4人
3.根據佔有的島嶼或是商業區上面的富饒標記拿錢，一個一元
4.開始照順位競標神明，後放的如果要放之前有的要高過，被超過的馬上拿回手並馬上放另外的位置，直到每個人一個位置(阿波羅可以多人放，要放就照順序)，標超過10就放標記在+10區
5.照神明順位上到下執行行動，執行完就放到順位軌最後面的位置，不同神明會有不同可執行行動
A.除阿波羅外都可以買生物卡並執行，不能存可一次買多張
B 波賽頓 免費一船，可花1/2/3買第2/3/4船，最多多買3艘，只能買在你島邊的沒敵人的海上，可花兩元蓋港口(海上戰爭相鄰格防禦時數值+1)，可多次，可花1元移動三格，中間可合併船隊或分散
C 戰神 免費一兵，可花1/2/3買第2/3/4兵，最多多買3，只能放自己島上，可花兩元蓋堡壘(戰爭防禦時數值+1)，可多次，可花1元移動到另一島(中間要每格都有船)，不能攻擊剩一島的人，除非打完就贏了
D 宙斯 免費一僧侶，多花4元可在買一隻(僧侶可降低競標的支付1元，最少還是一元)，可蓋寺廟，買生物卡少花一元，可花1元棄掉一張生物卡補新的
E 雅典娜 免費一哲學家，多花4元可在買一隻，四隻馬上棄掉蓋城市，可蓋大學，沒效果
F.阿波羅 多於一島拿一元，否則4元，然後第一個的可放一個富饒標記在一個島上
*移動遇到別人就戰鬥，每人丟骰然後加上士兵數，數字小的死一隻兵，平手都死一隻，之後防守方可撤退，在換進攻方撤退，都不退就繼續重複直到有人沒兵(要退到自己或中立的格子)
*當有人四種建築都有要馬上棄掉換成一個城市，大城市擁有四種建築物的功能
6.每人行動完回合結束，有兩大城市的人勝利
*2人遊戲1人使用兩個柱子，規則同四人，有三城市勝利
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Middleweight economic auction euro/war hybrid. Auctions are like Evo, Amun Re, Vegas Showdown etc.

Feels a lot like Antike, both thematically and in that it's seemingly easy to get within striking distance of winning, but difficult to finish the job - especially when you realise that some of the monster cards can seriously mess you up, and people can burn through the deck looking for just that. Pay attention to the monsters. 

Edit: After a few plays the pattern is that the endgame will come down to one of the non-leading players having to buy their way through the monster deck, hoping to draw one of a small number of cards that will stop the player who is about to win. As such the game largely comes down to luck of the draw, (not interesting), and furthermore problematic because if A burns their resources to stop B then player C who has not paid this cost can go on to win.

Would be improved by Antike style combat system.

If you're reduced to 1 island you are invincible. You can keep taking the extra income tokens, build up a massive income, build a metropolis, build a land army then use you cash reserves to cycle through the deck looking for the one that teleports your troops.

I really don't like the endgame of Cyclades - every game it comes down to paying to dig through the deck for one or two particular cards. Maybe they are at the top, maybe they are at the bottom - it might as well be one big dice roll.:yuk:

There is far too much luck for me to find this game interesting. The normal combat is also luck based (I'd prefer if it was Antike/Imperial style), but that's peanuts compared to the endgame. :zombie:

Also, most games, some players are forced to bid up things they have little to no use for just to stop so-and-so from getting it, but then they are crippled for next turn when a third party gets the benefit.:soblue:

Final gripe: hidden but trackable information.:yuk:

RATING: 7
Each round starts with an Amun-Re type auction for the 4 available actions (or skip out to get more money). Each of the actions allow you to build a different coloured building. Get one of each of those and you're halfway to winning, as you get to build a metropolis on one of your islands, and 2 wins it. One of the actions allow you to buy white cards. Get 4 of those and that's another way to build a metropolis. Or use the ship action to build up your ships, move them so as to create a convoy link between your island and someone elses, then use the army action to build armies and go take over someone else's island after some dice combat. Take over another already built metropolis and that's you're third way to getting there. With only one attack per turn, things aren't too chaotic, but each turn someone has that power and something will be happening. So it's a game of ensuring money supply, winning bids cheaply, planning any conquest a turn or more ahead with care, watching what everyone else is doing and being mindful of how each person is planning to get their second metropolis and acting earlier than the last minute to stop it. These are the things you're thinking through, but turns are pretty quick. The game is enjoyable enough, in that "everyone will be closing to winning, who am I going to stop" kind of way.

RATING: 6
This is a multi-player wargame in which each turn begins with an Amun-Re-style auction to determine what types of actions the players will get to execute on their turn.  The goal isn't solely about conquering; the first player to build up two of their territories to metropolises (or take over metropolises belonging to opponents) will win.  Because of the limited actions, only one player will get to attack each turn, which is an interesting feature.  In any case, I thought this was a well-designed game, but I don't really enjoy multi-player wargames, which is why my rating isn't higher.

(1 play)

zakoszulkowana

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I've only played twice so far, but here is my two cents:

-Great production Value
-A nice blend of Ameritrash with Euro gamer style
-Easy to pick up but not shallow


Success in the game will be primarily determined by your ability to bid on the right god at the right time. Being able to predict (and manipulate) your opponents behaviours will give you the upper hand. 

There is an element of luck in the game that will keep you on your toes. The dice differentials are very low so its unlikely this will make or break a well thought out strategy.

The cards can put a twist on things but accounting for this risk is part of the strategy as well. 

I recommend this game for those that bore with the mathematical steps of a game like Puerto Rico, but need more strategy and less luck from a game like Settlers of Catan. As a bonus the game looks fantastic, the pieces are well constructed, and the playing time is reasonable - enough to feel you've executed a complete strategy, but not so much that your slogging it out for hours.

RATING: 7.5
If you play Cyclades mainly as a euro you’ll probably lose. Yes, the bidding and the building aspects are important, but if you neglect fighting, positioning and drafting of mythological creature too much you’re in for a though time. Especially the creatures with their various special powers are far more important than one might suspect the first time playing, you got to make the most of the creatures really..

A single coincident can lead to a quick victory in Cyclades. It’s crucial to make the most of your turn – what can you do and what can you prevent other players from having? Timing is of essence in Cyclades and doing that move for victory is often a risk, exposing your self if failing. One bad move could ruin your chances of winning.

The rules are only – and just barely – medium complex, but I think Cyclades could be a hard game to master.

Two 4-player games so far..

RATING: 9
1/11/12 - I played this with 5 players recently and it was amazing. The auction mechanic combined with the ability to attack and build cities is an amazing combination. The components are beautiful and each color has different looking troops and ships. The artwork is also breathtaking. The game flows really well and I really enjoy it.

7/15/12 - This is my absolute favorite game. The choices and strategy of the game are really fun. You have to decide if you want to attack, if you want to move, if you want to build towards your metropolis, if you want to be first player to cycle through the cards, if you want to purchase help from the mythic deck, if you want to collect priests to help you in later rounds, if you need to block someone from attacking you, if you need to bid high on someone you don't need but someone else does so you can force them to spend extra money, how to get your resources, and how much you are willing to pay for all this. It's super fun and I can't wait to get the Hades expansion.

3/11/13 - Played again after a long time of sitting on the shelf and I really like it. Maybe it's because I won, I don't know. The game is really good but sometimes it's hard to coordinate attacks and ship movement for newer players.

RATING: 10
Perfect, concise military game with auction mechanics, special powers, and heated battles. On the surface, it seems like a strange mix of ideas, but it incorporates them into a fast, enjoyable game where tactics are valued over brawn. Never slow, always tense, about everything you could ask for in a game like this.

Edit: I think I've played this 4 times and it has an interesting "take down the leader" element to it, since the winning stroke can be won in 1-2 expertly executed rounds. So piling on the leader is common. That often leads to the 2nd place guy taking the lead, causing another pile on. Yet it somehow doesn't feel random or unnecessary. It all works and is never dull.

RATING: 7
Beautiful game. There's a lot of tense building up and bidding, feeling that at any time someone with a lot of money or the right monster-card can completely screw you over.

You don't have much control or defense, so it can be hard to make the right decisions. That can lead to a quick game with a lot of back and forth, or a slow ponderous game where everyone takes their time figuring out what the right amount to bid is and whether you can let the other player have this or that god.

Our first play was of the slow and ponderous kind, and at the end of the game I didn't feel like I had really done very much, but I have the feeling that if you play quickly and are willing to take some risks this can be an awesome build-and-fight game that can be played in a single evening, and there aren't many of those, especially not with a beautiful look and great miniatures like Cyclades.

Alex's and Allison's
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In general I enjoy games where you have military figures on the board so long as they don't get too fiddily and so long as meaningful combat isn't too random. 

In this game, you have to win the bid to worship the right god in order to take the action(s) associated with that god. The expansion adds a new god, hades, who covers up one of the god spots randomly, meaning the same actions aren't always available every turn. It's really fascinating and it sings with exactly 5. 

The minis are also really cool, even if they are a little pointless, as most of them have one-use effects and then vanish from the board. There can be situations where you get knocked out of a region by your opponent and you are unable to retake it just by virtue of not being able to win the bid for the move action. 

It's a double edged sword, as it is both part of the strategy and part of the frustration. Thankfully you can also win by getting a certain number of this one specific card, so you can try to switch gears for awhile if you start finding yourself outmatched militarily.

:star: Art and components
:star: Innovative mechanics
:star: Handles 5 or more players
:nostar: Good with min or max players
:star: Low time between turns
:star: Comfortable complexity
:nostar: Re-playability
:star::star::nostar: Enjoyment
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
An excellent game.  The miniatures make it seem like it is going to be Ameritrash and wall-to-wall combat (which a pretty tough sell in my group), but it really isn't.  It's a fascinating auction/area control type game with a bit of combat that is largely incidental, and probably could have been taken out of the game entirely.  
A complaint or two: the mini's are tiny, fragile, and kind of silly.  I think, if this becomes something we play more, I'll just get the wooden pieces.  Also, it is pretty heavy on the symbology.  Not a huge deal, but can be intimidating for some gamers who don't want a lot to memorize.  My group was not very excited to play this game at all while I was setting it up...eye rolls galore...but...
Once we got playing, it was fun.  Like real, visceral, engaging fun.  The auctions were loaded with cursing and laughing and dire proclamations of future revenge.  The best kind of reaction you can hope for in a game: emotional.  And as we moved our little men from island to island, circling the weaker civilizations, eyeing which monsters we could use to help defend or attack our neighbors, I was struck by how exciting and suspenseful the game was.  
Cyclades is a triumph for gaming.  Highly, highly recommend.

RATING: 7
Sept 2017: Better than expected! I'm lukewarm on dudes-on-a-map game as they tend to be too convoluted as a result of trying to be different than all the rest.

Very straightforward, perhaps a bit simplistic game play. I really like the straightforward objectives (just build two cities). The tech tree is quite simplified. Yes, there are lots of special powers, but most of them are used only once. 

What surprised me the most was the auction mechanism taken from [gameid=1159], which I found to work better in this game as (a) money is tighter so the auctions don't go on forever, and the things being auctioned off are actual actions and turn order -- the things have more of an impact on the game than the dinosaur parts in Evo.

RATING: 10
A multiplayer "waro" that doesn't make the player a hostage of the will of the others at the table. Fast setup, fast rounds and you can finish a light (but never shallow) 5-players civ game in under 2 hours. Marvelous art. And with just the right ammount of randomness. The designer got several elements right, like how the bidding works, the randomly available gods (actions), the low spread of the combat dice, the themed flavour of the creature deck, the reasonable compensation rules (Apollo and the one-island rule), the non-VP victory condition and the almost abscence of player elimination. A master class in modern boardgame design.

RATING: 7.5
Players represent one of the 5 major cities vying for control before ancient Greece had been consolidated as one state. Auctioning for role selection is central to this game, and how players get gold, assemble armies and fleets, move them, and build the 4 building types required to create a metropolis. It is also how to select the use of one of the three mythical creatures that can act as game changers, thwarting the best laid plans of other players. You must keep a close eye on each other, as the game plays quickly and the first with two metropolises will win. Combat is simple, and dice based. The game, early on, is one of building and fortifying your base, while preparing your strategy. The artwork is stunning, with simply one of the best box covers ever.

RATING: 9
FUN FAST MULTI PLAYER MYTHOLOGICAL LIGHT CIV BUILDING AND CONQUEST GAME
After two 5-P plays with my family I declare this to be an excellent family game.  The first play was slow as everyone absorbed the reasonably simple rule set.  The second game buzzed along quite quickly.  I was setting myself up for a win on the next turn when my youngest (9 YO) announced victory - there was one more player to go that turn but big sister could not avert little bro's victory.  There are a lot of things to think about and yuou need to watch the other players.  The 5-P game uis a hoot, I suspect 4-P will be just as good or better.  The mthological creatures seem like they will maintain variety of play.  My initial impression is that this is a truly top notch light-middleweight game.

Have played three more time with my gaming group.  The last two plays were 4P knock down dragouts that lasted 3-4 hours each.  Two factors for long game length.  First -smart competitive players ready to knock out the leader, often via wicked bidding wars,  Second in 4P game one god always missing, often Ares or Poseidon, resulting in multi turn set ups for critical attackes.  Ultimate compliment from the moat Euro-ish guy in the group, despite game lasting from 8:00 to 11:30 PM = it did not seem long at all, totally immersed for every minute.
[Holidays 2010]

RATING: 7.51
Light competitive game. In each turn the players bid to take on different roles. The roles allow them to conduct certain actions, building cities, gathering or moving armies, assembling philosophers or priests. These things allow players to create metropoli, or to capture them from other players. When one player captures two they win the game.
The bidding mechanism, role selection, and manner in which navies transport armies, are all clever little mechanics that present a challenge. Though all of them are borrowed from different games the way they are assembled is quite interesting.
The game has, as many Euro style games do, a rather sharp end-game. It kicks in rather suddenly, bringing the game to a rapid end without much opportunity for fortunes to swing back and forth.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
An interesting merger of a Euro-style auction mechanic with moving armies about the board and fighting by rolling dice. I think it's a good game - it looks absolutely beautiful too - but these days I rarely find myself wanting to play it. The various different mythological creatures keep each game different - but Pegasus is overpowered (not game-breakingly so, but definitely in the sense that even a first-time player needs to be told that it exists so that they can plan for it). The rules, which do a good job on most things, also do a woefully inadequate job of explaining exactly how the creatures work (there is a separate reference sheet with all of them on, but it is far too sketchy), meaning that either a quick decision on how to interpret them, or looking up rules questions on BGG, is necessary.

It's still an excellent game, though - just not one that's often on my "I want to play this tonight" list. In fact, we haven't played it since at least 2013, and I can't say I'm in a rush to play again.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
05-06-2014. Rated after one play. I like this game a lot. Cyclades is often compared to KEMET, which I own. In contrast with Kemet, attacking is more expensive and less rewarded in Cyclades making the game more tactical and less opportunistic. 

Combat itself is not extremely tense in Cyclades, just number of guys + die roll. Kemet has great card-driven combat system, which allows for some neat tricks. 

What for me is a big improvement of Cyclades over Kemet, is that Kemet has a poorer action selection mechanism in which everyone selects 5 actions in turn and competes for special abilities. The tension is Kemet is not in the worker placement, but in the combat.

In Cyclades in contrast, there are 5 actions available that are auctioned off, making it very tense because if you do not get Ares, you cannot attack. If you do not get Poseidon, you cannot build or move ships. 

This is were Cyclades really shines, although I think both games are different enough to warrant purchase. Also, there is a neat expansion available which allows you to mix both games.

RATING: 7.5
Amazing game!  Looks like a wargame, but it's really not - there's more the threat of potential attack than much attacking, and the mythical monsters add enough surprise so you're never sure if you have a secure defense.  Turns go really fast, and while it can take a little time to figure out how high you can bid in the auction, the calculation is much faster than say Power Grid.  This will probably Jones theory Vegas Showdown for me - quite similar in terms of the auctions, but more interesting interaction in terms of the game board dynamics and in vying for turn order.

Update: Lowered from 8.5 to 7.5 - while fun, there are some weird interactions that can come up that decrease the fun factor for me.  The auctions are much more about guessing how much your opponent is willing to bid and then starting that bid at or above that - there is often very little outbidding, especially at 3 players.  I would actually recommend avoiding this with 3 players.  Still good but not itching to play it like before.

RATING: 7.5
I don't see anybody talking about this game anymore; it seems to have been overshadowed by Kemet.  Kemet may be a better game, but I feel they should really be so directly compared as they often are; Cyclades' auction-based action selection makes it really unique.  Some people may be put off by the fact that only one person each round may attack, while only one may move ships, etc., and the abruptness of the game end.  Others, however, will love the feeling that no player is really going to have a runaway lead in this game, due to the fact that victory always seems to be a few unchecked moves away for everyone once the game has gotten going.

This game has beautiful (and unnecessary; there's some great stuff even on the backs of board segments) art.

RATING: 7
A great game. Good mix of euro mechanics and ameri interaction and sensible winning condition (no VPs!). One of the best battle resolution mechanism, which while extremely simple, makes luck firmly secondary to skill. Finally, best catch-up mechanic I've seen, making you fight till the end as you [b]always[/b] have reasonable chances of victory, at least with four or five players. Its maybe even too strong - if you're attacked early and limited to one island in a game of four or more players, you're paradoxically on a good way to victory.

Why not a higher rating? Nowadays I play mostly euros, or at least more complex games.  I will still pull this out within a heartbeat if confronted with less experienced players, though - it's a perfect gateway for conflict oriented groups.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6

I haven't played base game Cyclades for a while as the group I'm playing such games with combined it with Hades expansion. Until after half a year or so I decided I was fed up with it and refused to play it anymore. It's hard to say if the problems I've had with it were group related (groupthink) or expansion related - I can for time being believe some groups having no problems with it, however if a group has certain approach the Hades expansion makes it much more pronounced.

Problems of Hades: Basically Hades allows for more attacking options (yes, people cried, we want more DoaM action) and it gives heroes and stuff and more stuff. Problem is all these things go in tangent to what pushes the game forward. The game finishes when somebody controls 2 metropolises - more attacking makes it easier to take them over. But who is going to build them? Ehm. Yeah. Heroes seem cool, but they cost upkeep and that's money which will not go into what builds a metropolis. Sure most heroes have a special power that makes it easier to build a metropolis, but given their cost I'd say it doesn't pay off the money and effort put into them. And they do another thing: with upkeep they ask for steady income, so players are focusing more on getting territory and trade routes to build an economic base, neither of which pushes the game towards conclusion. Those special cards and whatnot are just stuff for sake of stuff hence distraction. Then we get to Hades. What seems cool - more attacking - actually isn't as it makes easier to take over built metropolises, hence: nobody is in rush to build them, instead they're putting money in more armies and gaining new territories. End effect: Hades evens the swingy nature of the base game at the cost of making the game long, samey and outstaying its welcome. And paradoxically - more attacking actually pronounces economic nature of the game.

Titans does everything right where Hades went wrong. Hades as a God was only occasionally available, hence you needed to sit on money to get it when he came around. Titans work the other way - these units enable moves every turn (unless you're on Apollo), hence people have more control over their money and can spend it more accordingly to proper needs. The main dude is of course Chronos who by his power over time shortens the game - basically he gives free buildings. And some buildings also start the game on the board. And first two metropolises build even get a special bonus. So there's incentive to build them quickly, but with buildings entering play, they just happen, very soon actually. The map itself is a good idea - as with titan units movement is pronounced and much easier. Fleets now have a different role - one of gaining you upkeep with rich small (uninhabitable) islands and richer trade routes. With them it's much easier to build and economic base than it used to be. And then there are relics which are the new, improved heroes - they don't cost upkeep, no, they give you money (which seems so obvious it's weird how it was missed before). Basically Titans is a corrective of Hades  - instead of expansions that adds more and more stuff which just distracts from what pushes the game forward and makes it drag, oh so much, this expansions puts everything it has to make the game run faster. Everything in Titans is in this or other way connected to building metropolises or taking them from other players (either you get buildings or you get money).

So far we only played teams, so I'm not sure yet of how it is to play solo. And I'd need to play base game again to see how much of the crime of Hades is already imprinted in the base. Yes, this could have been a stand alone. For those saying it moves Cylades too near to Kemet I'd say: Hallelujah. I hate Kemet's tech tree (and tacky board art), but like other parts. Cyldes Titans is basically for me Kemet without those parts I find annoying.

RATING: 7.5
Played 3 games with 2P, and 1 game with 3P. While Cyclades is a hybrid game, auctions are still the primary focus, and battles are simply a means to an end. I really love how each god is equally important to victory, so there is always a fierce contest each round. Thankfully, the map is cleverly constrained so battles to take over and expand territories are inevitable. Combine the tight gameplay with gorgeous components and you've got a great game.

There are 2 downsides I can think of. The first is the anticlimactic end as the winner can be predicted 2 or 3 rounds before the game actually finishes. Secondly, the one 3-player game I tried outlasted its welcome, which soured my impressions of Cyclades somewhat. I think this has to do with the fact that only 2 of the 4 variable gods are available each turn, which restricts players' options and slows down the game. I've lowered my ratings for Cyclades over time, but this is still a neat game to play when I'm in the mood for a more combative game.

Nem könnyű ezt a játékot értékelnem. Jó mechanizmusok tényleg jól összegyúrva, de mindent felülír, hogy csak egy nyertese lehet a játéknak és nem igazán lehet helyezéseket felállítani. A játékosok istenek kegyeit keresik egy Amun-Re-ben megismert licitmechanizmus nagyon kicsi módosításával. Adott isten segítségével különböző akciók lehetségesek a körben. Mindig lesz egy játékos, aki nem tud segítséget kérni a körben, ő viszont pénzt és későbbi jövedelmet szerezhet. Kellemes része ez a játéknak. Az akciók közben lehetőség van különböző teremtmények felbérlésére, akik nagyon színesítik a játékmenetet és erős behatással lehetnek a játékra. A térkép kör alakú, ahol vízen és szárazföldön lehet harcolni. A csata nem túlbonyolított, nem túl vészes szerencsefaktorral kitalált. A cél két metropolisz felhúzása. Ez több módon összejöhet. 4 filozófus kártya beadásával, 4 különböző épület felhúzásával vagy egyszerűen csak másénak az elfoglalásával. Elsőre nekem egy hibája van a Cycladesnek, de az sajnos óriási. Egy nyertes van, a többiek vesztesek. Legtöbbször jól érzékelhető ki áll nyerésre, ennek megakadályozására feláldozza valaki magát így ők ketten nem nyerhetnek, nyer más. 3 játékosnál ez nagyon kellemetlen lehet, de nekünk 4 játékos esetében is egyértelmű volt a végkimenetel. Talán 2 játékos esetén lenne ez a legkevésbé fájdalmas dolog, de ketten viszont a jó licitmechanizmusnak nem lenne semmi értelme a játékban. Szóval számomra így nem jó játék a Cyclades minden erénye ellenére.

RATING: 7
[i]Fun Game, but Suffers Heavily from Weird End-Game and Kingmaker Issues[/i]

Best with ? Players

I like this game, especially with the expansion -- the mix of auctions and combat provide the blend of economy and combat that I love in games (probably due to my RTS gaming roots).

You can build stuff, you can expand, and you can bid perfectly on every auction... but if you do not take your opponents into account and defend yourself, it will all be taken away from you in an instant.

Between the combat and the special card powers, there are quite a few paths to victory, and this game challenges you to successfully valuate who is in the lead now, who will be next turn, the turn after that, and how they will get there -- and then not just "outperform them" as you would do in a low-interaction game, but [i]beat them[/i]. That's my kind of thing.

Also, I find it hilarious that they felt it was necessary to include unique plastic miniature molds for mythological creatures that are on the board for ONE TURN! Instead of just some stupid counter or cardboard standup or something. That's some shit I haven't seen since the 90s!

That said, I wish the plastic saw more use, as it's really cool looking and then just goes away, doesn't seem right

(3 Design + 4 Enjoyment)

[hr]After a few plays, I think the end-game feels weird. Unless you get "eliminated" early, you will most likely find yourself in a position to win, along with other players, and the last turn feels almost like a tie-breaker in itself, ripe for kingmaking whether you try to win yourself (if you have the clear initiative other players will have to collude to stop you, empowering someone else) or try to stop others (another mole that can win this turn will pop up)

Also, the kingmaking and bean counting at the end is  probably a nightmare with good memories, open-money or notes, as the information about how much money people have is theoretically completely trackable despite the rules saying to hide it (a sin in my eyes) Design docked.

Another "self balancing" multi-player wargame that requires everyone to beat on the leader in order normalize the game.  Best way to win is to not care about losing.  Let the other people do the work and sneak a win from second place.  Pretty typical stuff.  

There is real strategy here.  Here's what you have to do to get anything done: earn money and discounts (from auctions), win the auction to get you ships together, win the auction to make guys and move them on ships, then roll the dice to see if it was worth it. It takes so long to do anything in this game that the strategy is to catch everyone with their pants down and time a victory set-up so that no one can resist it (otherwise it is a cycle of pain).  

Everyone is playing a "don't hit me, hit him game" as the game gracefully forces an end condition. Best to stay out of people's way in the first half of the game, no need to do anything too productive making yourself a target.  Rather, build up your efficiency.

I will say that thematically it is cool, and the art is awesome.  If I were 14 this game would be amazing. If some teenage kid wanted to play this with me, I would gladly, but the likelihood of that happening is about zero.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3

**Update: From 6 down to 3 and into the street. There is little joy from what you accomplish in this game. Playing it cutthroat it goes gruellingly long, with no one really accomplishing anything.

Leaves you with this Empty feeling.

Been having so much fun with this one. Excellent combination of bidding and war: a hybrid of Eurogame and Ameritrash (Eurotrash). Also thinking of house ruling the Pegasis power down quite a bit. The effect of these house rules is to bend the game a tiny bit to our desires. Without these house rules, the game can tend to make huge, quick swings in power, and we prefer a slower, more evenly paced game - but that's just us.

RATING: 8
Gods, they can be fickle, they can be angry, they can be generous, but most of all, they can be expensive!!!!! Cyclades is a sort of war game in which you try to buy the favor of several costly gods by out bidding your unworthy heathen opponents. If you succeed the gods will reward your patronage with gifts of warriors, ships, philosophers and other goodies. If you fail to outbid your opponents then you'll have to just pray to Apollo who will give you a few bucks and maybe a cornucopia if you're lucky. Then you take your rewards and honor the gods by murdering everyone in sight! Fun! You also get to enlist the aid of several mythological beasts who help you do various things,including helping you murder everyone in sight. Turns out killing in the name of gods is a hell of a lot of fun, now I finally understand the appeal of the crusades! I should also mention that they did a god damned awesome job with the components in this game..superb! And the god bidding is way more fun than I thought. great game, I swear to god(s)

RATING: 7
This is an interesting mix of auction and area control game with some very, very light battle mechanics.  The auction is the bulk of the game but what you are auctioning off are actions in the area control "arena".

I actually really, really like this game mechanics- and design-wise.  The auction is very well designed, the order of the gods changes each turn and the order dictates the order of their use and the earlier you go in one turn the later you go in the next.  Also, being outbid on one god tile prohibits you from jumping back onto the same god's auction track.

The mythical creatures also provide a great way to diversify the game and place more pressure on early picks in the auction even if that particular god isn't your ideal choice.  I also really like the design choice to prevent player elimination by disallowing conquering of a player's last island unless it provides you a win.  This combined with the 4-gold Apollo bonus for having only one island are great catch up mechanics.

All of this makes for an incredibly well designed game...with some really faulty end-game goals that brings it down quite a bit. For an area control game, this one really discourages player interaction past the auction phase which is a big problem for me.  Outside of the powers of some of the mythical creatures, combat with other players "the honest way" requires so much time and resources it doesn't seem worth it.  The big problem is that with multiple players harassing each other usually it is the quiet person who takes a lead in the game while they are unmolested.  Then this person is usually just stonewalled in getting their second metropolis which just delays them for a few turns while they collect more resources and others spend all theirs to stop them.

One criticism I do feel is unfair is I've heard it put down because of the amount of time it takes to "do so little" on a turn but I think that's because people don't look at the area control aspect as ancillary or reactionary to the auction phase.  This is at its core an auction game and the auctions are deep, complex, and exciting and don't even take the time an auction in Power Grid would, for example.  But when taking the actions you won in auction you make little ripples in the game at a time and if someone looks at the giant board full of islands, troops, and fleets and expects this to be a sweeping area control or war game they are going to be disappointed with the little bit they get to do during that phase.

I would have loved all the game play of this game with a different objective, I just feel that they don't fit together very nicely and it can kind of spoil it towards the end game when you notice the problems with it.  I still really like the game for the journey though.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
One game with 3 players and another one with only 2.

Game components are obviously excellent. Great art work once again from Miguel Coimbra (although I like Giants better). The auction mechanism is pretty good like in Amun Re or Vegas Showdown but that's all because once you're done with the auction everything else can be pure chaos because of, especially, the cards. Cards can ruin 3 or 4 turns in a single action.

But my major complaint goes for two strong reasons: first of all the fact that the player who has the most money has the advantage to get even more money - the possibilities of a player to recover are poor. Even if a player can recover from a serious defeat the game is not very fun anymore because it takes too much time for that player to get back into the game. The second reason has to do with the bash the leader feeling. It's obvious that once all players know that someone goes ahead in the game, that player has to be controlled by other's actions. This is something I don't like in games.

I can give it another try but I'm not sure I'll change my opinion about it.

(T)

RATING: 9
LIKE
+ Great art and components.
+ Biding mechanic is tense and thrilling.
+ No player elimination and come back are possible.
+ You can always see what is coming. To problem is having the will (or money!) to do it.
DISLIKE
- Without the 2 metropolis at the beginning of your turn rule, endings are anti-climatic.
- Even though you always move toward the end game, progression (especially movement) can feel slow.
- Certain creatures at the right moment can win the game.
VERDICT
The perfect ameritrash and euro blend in in less than 90 minutes. Truly epic feel. Most of the flaws are fixed by the Hades expansion (I never play without it now).

RATING: 8
This is a "first impressions" rating after a single play with 5 players.  It remains to be seen if my rating will change with further plays!  Right after the game ended, a good friend of mine commented that this game could have been custom designed for me - a compelling theme, gorgeous components, clever resource management, a bit of conflict, plenty of player interaction, and the same design team that created one of my favourite games of all time, "Mr. Jack".  And he was absolutely correct!  But it's not perfect, of course.  My biggest complaint was that the game end came rather suddenly just when I felt I was starting to make some progress in the game, which made it feel a little anticlimactic.  Sure, the end game conditions keep the game length very reasonable, but this is the type of game I don't mind spending longer on.  (In contrast to these statements, one of the game designers has commented that games tend to be longer with more experienced players, since they learn how to better interfere with their opponents' victory plans.)  Also, I fell behind early with my income, and spent the rest of the game picking up the scraps left by everyone else.  I would have liked to see a bit more money in play - perhaps even 1 or 2 gold pieces added each game turn to the regular income - although I don't know if this would simply result in bigger auctions.  My hope would be that a bit more income would result in a little more ebb and flow in a game that feels somewhat too static considering all the amazing armies and ships that are in play.  I wonder if these problems were partly a result of playing with 5 players.  Perhaps with 3 or 4, I would feel like I was able to accomplish more in the game.  [Edit: After trying a 2-player game, I can vouch for the fact that it plays very well with 2 and doesn't have the same issues that I just discussed above, although I wish I could have a similar experience with a higher number of players.]  But don't get me wrong - this is a fun and very compelling game, and I can't wait to play it again!  And the production value is nothing short of spectacular.  The fact that each player has different sculpts for their armies and even their ships is astounding!  And I'm enjoying painting up those 5 mythological creatures...  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 3.5/5  Total: 8/10

RATING: 6.75
Hm another hybrid of wargame and euro by Mr Cathala. Something like [gameid=33107]. Looks like more successful attempt, and may be enjoyable but... I hardly feel urge to try it again more than one or two times.

I must admit that Cyclades nicely mix bidding system with changing order of play, dontime is low, game is quick, high-quality components are very nice, and in overall it look like serious attempt to create short, intense and interesting game. But I cannot decide what doesn't fit: Too many euro-ish elements? Effectively winning the game due to properly handled bidding and building diminishes importance of war. But you can war -- but war usually are devastating and bring not too much gain (in fact, this is like in reality, through this game ask you for some conflict and then makes it unsatisfactory). Also, too many plans simply evolve from results of bidding.

Of course, this is biased opinion: Games that require you to build proper number of items and army units and then finally use them in final blows are not my favorites. It is hard to focus on building while your plans can be disrupted at any moment but some sudden attack. But something simply doesn't fit here. So, try first before you buy.

EDIT: After second play I'm upgrading the rating a bit -- three-player game is quite satysfying.

RATING: 9
Manages to perfectly blend gameplay with theme. The rules are simple (contained within five pages) but there's still a lot going on in this game. The basic premise is that the player controls various Greek gods who in turn bestow various powers, which then enable the player to develop their civilization across the Cyclades islands - the first player to develop two metropolises wins the game. For example, Poseidon controls a player's fleets and ports, Ares controls their armies and fortresses, Zeus controls their priests and temples etc. As only one player can have access to a certain god's powers per cycle (round), tactical bidding takes place to see who earns the privilege. There's also a number of creatures from Greek mythology whose services can be acquired and these also provide greater depth of decision making to the game. The artwork and overall presentation of the game is excellent, which means that as well as being challenging to play, it's also visually appealing. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Cyclades has been on my wishlist for a while but I was concerned that the auction wouldn't be a good basis for a Dudes on a Map game. I was completely wrong as by keeping almost all the action on the game board, limiting the aggressive actions available and not having special player powers players can concentrate on the effect of their actions on the overall game state. It just works so smoothly and is a brilliant piece of design. I was also concerned that the end game would be awful but it wasn't too bad. As the new player I was the weakest link and made any number of errors but I came away with an appreciation for the jostling necessary to set yourself up to clinch victory before anyone else can. I'm almost guaranteed to pick this up next year.

RATING: 8.5

Mostly 1 god is doing the heavy lifting so I can see these moves working in a multiplayer game.  Your best laid plans are quickly vanquished so you better have a plan B at all times.
